The Three Muslim Views on Allah's Place
Maturidi enumerates three Muslim views on Allah's place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three divergent positions on Allah's relationship to place that emerged among early Muslim theologians, and the scriptural proofs each group cited.

Core Idea
Three wrong paths on Allah's place: literal throne-sitting, omnipresence, or metaphorical denial.

Before we can appreciate the nuanced middle path of the Ash'ari and Maturidi scholars, we must first map out the landscape of earlier opinions. The passage from Imam Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid catalogues three distinct views among Muslims regarding how to speak of Allah's location. Each view claims scriptural support, yet each falls short of preserving divine transcendence. This lesson introduces those views and their primary proof texts.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification passage
Read the Arabic passage that lists the three groups. Note how each group is introduced with 'faminhum' (some of them).
The passage uses a clear enumerative structure.
2
Identify each group and its claim
List the three groups: those who say He is on the Throne as a seat, those who say He is everywhere, and those who negate spatial description except metaphorically.
Each group cites specific Qur'anic verses.
3
Examine the proof texts
For each group, note the verses they use. For the first group, verses about angels carrying the Throne and istiwa; for the second, the 'fourth of three' verse; for the third, the metaphorical interpretation.
The first group uses 'thumma istawa' to argue He came to the Throne after not being on it.
4
Reflect on the problem
Ask yourself: what theological error does each view risk? The first leads to anthropomorphism, the second to pantheism, the third to metaphorical denial of attributes.

ويتوسط الأشعري في بيان العرش والاستواء ، فيقول ابن عساكر : وكذلك قالت النجارية : إن الباري سبحانه بكل مكان من غير حلول ولا جهة ، وقالت الحشوية المجسمة : إنه سبحانه حال في العرش ، وأن العرش مكان له ، وهو جالس عليه ، فسلك طريقة بينها فقال : كان ولا مكان ، فخلق العرش والكرسي ولم يحتج إلى مكان ، وهو بعد خلق المكان كما كان قبل خلقة . وإلى مثل ذلك أيضاً يذهب الماتريدي، فنقرأ من كتاب التوحيد : ثم اختلف أهل الإسلام في القول بالمكان ، فمنهم من زعم أنه يوصف بأنه على العرش والعرش عندهم السرير المحمول بالملائكة المحفوف : وَيَحْمِلُ عَرْشَ رَبِّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ يَوْمَئِذٍ ثَمَانِيَةٌ . وقوله : وَتَرَى المَلائِكَةُ حَافِّينَ مِنْ حَوْلِ العرش . وقوله : الَّذِينَ يَحْمِلُونَ العَرْشَ وَمَنْ حَوْلَه . واحتجوا للقول به بقوله : الرَّحمن عَلَى العَرْشِ اسْتَوَى ويقولون : هو صار إليه بعد أن لم يكن ؛ لقوله : ثُمَّ اسْتَوى عَلَى العَرْشِ .... ومنهم من يقول : هو بكل مكان بقوله : ما يكون مِنْ نَجْوَى ثَلَاثَةٍ إِلَّا هُوَ رَابِعُهُم ... ومنهم من قال بنفي الوصف بالمكان ، وكذلك بالأمكنة كلها إلا على مجاز اللغة بمعنى المحافظ ، والقائم بها ..... قال الشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله : وجملة ذلك أن إضافة كلية الأشياء إليه ، وإضافته عز وجل إليها يخرج مخرج الوصف له بالعلو والرفعة ، ومخرج التعظيم له والجلال الأصل فيه أن الله سبحانه كان ولا مكان، وجائز ارتفاع الأمكنة وبقاؤه على ما كان ، فهو على ما كان ، وكان على ما عليه الآن ، جمل عن التغير والزوال والاستحالة والبطلان ؛ إذ ذلك وأما الأصل عندنا في ذلك أن الله تعالى قال : لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ أمارات الحدث ، فنفى عن نفسه شبه خلقه ، وقد بينا أنه في فعله وصفته متعال عن الأشباه ؛ فيجب القول ' الرحمن على العرش استوى على ما جاء به التنزيل ، وثبت ذلك في العقل ، ثم لا نقطع تأويله على شيء ، لاحتمال غيره مما ذكرنا ونو من وكذلك في كل أمر ثبت التنزيل فيه نحو الرؤية وغير والإيمان بما أراده من غير تحقيق على شيء
Al-Ash'ari took a middle path in the explanation of the Throne (al-‘Arsh) and the Establishment (al-Istiwa). Ibn 'Asakir says: Likewise, al-Najjariyya said that the Creator, glorified is He, is in every place without indwelling (hulul) or direction (jiha). And the Hashwiyya al-Mujassima said that He is indwelling in the Throne, and that the Throne is a place for Him, and He is sitting upon it. So he followed a middle way between them and said: He was without a place, then He created the Throne and the Chair and did not need a place, and He after creating place is as He was before creation. And Maturidi also goes to that effect. We read from Kitab al-Tawhid: Then the people of Islam differed concerning the saying about place. Some of them claimed that He is described as being upon the Throne, and the Throne with them is the couch carried by the encircling angels: 'and those who bear the Throne of your Lord above them on that day, eight' (al-Haqqa 69:17), and His saying: 'And you see the angels encircling around the Throne' (al-Zumar 39:75), and His saying: 'Those who bear the Throne and those around it' (Ghafir 40:7). And they argued for that with His saying: 'The Most Merciful established Himself upon the Throne' (TaHa 20:5), and they say: He came to it after He was not, because of His saying: 'Then He established Himself upon the Throne' (al-A'raf 7:54). And some of them say: He is in every place with His saying: 'There is no secret counsel of three except that He is the fourth of them' (al-Mujadila 58:7). And some of them said by negating the description with place, and likewise with all places except metaphorically in the sense of preservation and overseeing... Abu Mansur (al-Maturidi), may Allah have mercy on him, said: The sum of that is that the attribution of all things to Him, and His attribution to them, takes the form of describing Him with loftiness and highness, and of magnifying Him and majesty. The principle in that is that Allah, glorified is He, was without a place, and it is possible for places to cease while He remains as He was. So He is as He was, and He was as He is now, [far] from change, passing, transformation, and nullification; because that... And the principle with us in that is that Allah, exalted, said: 'There is nothing like Him' (al-Shura 42:11) [as] signs of createdness, and He negated from Himself similarity to His creation. And we have explained that He in His action and attribute is transcendent above likenesses. So it is necessary to say: 'The Most Merciful established Himself upon the Throne' as it came in revelation, and that is established in reason, then we do not cut off its interpretation on any one thing, because of the possibility of other interpretations from what we have mentioned and the like. And likewise in every matter in which revelation is established, such as the vision and other things, we believe in what He intended without determining a specific meaning.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage classifies the differing views on the issue of al-makan (place) and al-istiwa (establishment) and presents the Maturidi-Ash'ari middle path. It begins by quoting Ash'ari's position as reported by Ibn 'Asakir: Ash'ari rejected both the Najjariyya's claim that Allah is in every place without hulul (indwelling) and the Hashwiyya Mujassima's anthropomorphism that He sits on the Throne. Instead, Ash'ari said: 'He was without place, then created the Throne and the Chair and did not need a place, and He after creating place is as He was before creation.' Maturidi also adopts this view. Then Maturidi presents the three Muslim factions: (1) Those who say He is on the Throne as a physical seat, citing verses about angels carrying it and the istiwa verse, and they claim He came to the Throne after not being on it; (2) Those who say He is everywhere, citing the verse about being with the creation in their councils; (3) Those who negate spatial description altogether, except metaphorically as 'preservation.' Then Maturidi gives his own conclusion: The principle is that Allah was without place, and places are contingent; He is not subject to change. The ultimate principle is the Quranic verse 'Laysa kamithlihi shay' (Nothing is like Him), which negates similarity. Therefore, we must affirm the verse 'al-Rahman 'ala al-arsh istawa' as it came in revelation, and it is rationally sound, but we do not settle on a single interpretation because multiple interpretations are possible. This method of tafwid (suspending interpretation) is applied to all ambiguous revealed texts.

Key Terms
عرش
استواء
مكان
تشبيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All three views are equally valid interpretations of scripture.
Correction: The passage does not validate any; it merely reports the views. Later, Ash'ari and Maturidi present a corrective middle path.

Checkpoint
Which verse did the first group use to argue that Allah came to the Throne after not being on it?
A) 'The Most Merciful established Himself upon the Throne' (TaHa 20:5)
B) 'Then He established Himself upon the Throne' (al-A'raf 7:54)
C) 'And you see the angels encircling around the Throne' (al-Zumar 39:75)
D) 'There is no secret counsel of three...' (al-Mujadila 58:7)

Key Takeaway
Early Muslims held three conflicting views on Allah's place – literal throne, omnipresence, or metaphorical – each with scriptural support, but all problematic for divine transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'The Most Merciful is established upon the Throne', what image forms in your mind? Are you willing to discipline your imagination and leave the modality (kayfiyya) unknown? What specific habit will you adopt to avoid mental picturing?
?
The fact that early Muslims disagreed on whether Allah occupies a place—does that unsettle your confidence in the clarity of the Quran? How do you reconcile this disagreement with your belief that the Quran is clear? Will you investigate further or remain content with the disagreement?
?
Which of the three views on Allah's place do you find yourself instinctively leaning toward? What does that inclination reveal about your heart's attachment to a particular mental image of Allah? Are you willing to sacrifice that mental comfort for the sake of affirming His absolute transcendence?

Divine Transcendence

Al-Ash'ari's Middle Path on the Throne
Ibn 'Asakir reports Ash'ari's middle path on place and Throne.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari formulated a middle path between anthropomorphism and denial of attributes by affirming Allah's transcendence of place while maintaining His action of creating the Throne.

Core Idea
He was without place, then created the Throne without needing it; He remains as He was.

After seeing the extreme views on Allah's relationship to place, Imam al-Ash'ari proposed a nuanced statement that avoids both anthropomorphism and empty metaphor. Reported by Ibn 'Asakir, his position is succinct: Allah existed without a place, then created the Throne and the Chair without any need for them, and after creation He is as He was before. Maturidi also adheres to this principle. This lesson examines that concise formulation and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the Ash'ari statement
Focus on Ibn 'Asakir's report of Ash'ari's words. Notice how it begins by rejecting two extremes before stating the middle path.
Ash'ari first criticizes the Najjariyya and Hashwiyya views.
2
Analyze the key phrase: 'kan wa la makan'
Ash'ari says 'He was without place.' This affirms that place is not an attribute of Allah; He existed before all creation.
3
Understand 'after creating place as He was before'
Ash'ari asserts that creating the Throne did not change Allah's relation to place; He remains transcendent. The Throne is a created object, not a dwelling.
4
Connect to Maturidi
The text says Maturidi also goes to that effect. This signals agreement between the two schools on this fundamental point.

Commentary
This passage classifies the differing views on the issue of al-makan (place) and al-istiwa (establishment) and presents the Maturidi-Ash'ari middle path. It begins by quoting Ash'ari's position as reported by Ibn 'Asakir: Ash'ari rejected both the Najjariyya's claim that Allah is in every place without hulul (indwelling) and the Hashwiyya Mujassima's anthropomorphism that He sits on the Throne. Then Maturidi gives his own conclusion: The principle is that Allah was without place, and places are contingent; He is not subject to change. How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray, do you catch yourself imagining Allah as being 'above' or in a certain direction? How does knowing that He was without place and remains unchanged challenge that habit? What will you do to train your heart to think of Him as transcendent beyond space?
?
If Allah does not need the Throne—the greatest of His creation—then how much less does He need your worship, your deeds, or your repentance? Yet He commands them. Does your obedience stem from a sense that He 'needs' it, or from pure gratitude? Examine your motive today.
?
The Najjariyya made Allah 'everywhere' without place; the Hashwiyya confined Him to a throne. Which of these errors do you find yourself leaning toward in your own thoughts about Allah's closeness or distance? Ask Allah to purify your understanding of His transcendence.

Maturidi's Principle: Affirmation without Ta'yin
Maturidi states his principle for understanding istiwa and similar attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam al-Maturidi's methodological principle for handling verses about Allah's attributes: affirm them as revealed, but do not fix a single interpretation because of the possibility of other meanings, based on the principle that nothing is like Him.

Core Idea
Say 'al-Rahman 'ala al-arsh istawa' as revealed, but do not specify how.

Imam al-Maturidi builds upon the shared Ash'ari- Maturidi foundation by providing a detailed methodological principle for dealing with attributes like istiwa. He begins by affirming that Allah was without place and that places are contingent. Then he grounds his approach in the Qur'anic verse 'There is nothing like Him,' which negates similarity. Consequently, he argues that we must recite the verse as revealed, affirm its truth in reason, but not settle on a single interpretation because alternative interpretations remain possible. This principle, known as tafwid, is applied to all ambiguous revealed texts, such as the vision of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read Maturidi's conclusion
Start from 'The sum of that is...' Read the entire passage. Notice how it first restates the principle that Allah was without place.
This builds on the earlier classification.
2
Identify the foundational principle: 'laysa kamithlihi shay'
Maturidi grounds his approach in the verse that negates any likeness to Allah. This is the basis for rejecting anthropomorphism.
3
Understand the method: affirmation without ta'yin
Maturidi says we must say 'al-Rahman 'ala al-arsh istawa' as it came in revelation, and it is rationally sound, but we do not cut off its interpretation to one meaning because other interpretations are possible.
This is tafwid (suspending definitive interpretation).
4
Generalize the rule
Maturidi extends this principle to all similar revealed matters, such as the vision of Allah. We believe what He intended without determining a specific meaning.

ويتوسط الأشعري في بيان العرش والاستواء ، فيقول ابن عساكر : وكذلك قالت النجارية : إن الباري سبحانه بكل مكان من غير حلول ولا جهة ، وقالت الحشوية المجسمة : إنه سبحانه حال في العرش ، وأن العرش مكان له ، وهو جالس عليه ، فسلك طريقة بينها فقال : كان ولا مكان ، فخلق العرش والكرسي ولم يحتج إلى مكان ، وهو بعد خلق المكان كما كان قبل خلقة . وإلى مثل ذلك أيضاً يذهب الماتريدي، فنقرأ من كتاب التوحيد : ثم اختلف أهل الإسلام في القول بالمكان ، فمنهم من زعم أنه يوصف بأنه على العرش والعرش عندهم السرير المحمول بالملائكة المحفوف : وَيَحْمِلُ عَرْشَ رَبِّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ يَوْمَئِذٍ ثَمَانِيَةٌ . وقوله : وَتَرَى المَلائِكَةُ حَافِّينَ مِنْ حَوْلِ العرش . وقوله : الَّذِينَ يَحْمِلُونَ العَرْشَ وَمَنْ حَوْلَه . واحتجوا للقول به بقوله : الرَّحمن عَلَى العَرْشِ اسْتَوَى ويقولون : هو صار إليه بعد أن لم يكن ؛ لقوله : ثُمَّ اسْتَوى عَلَى العَرْشِ .... ومنهم من يقول : هو بكل مكان بقوله : ما يكون مِنْ نَجْوَى ثَلَاثَةٍ إِلَّا هُوَ رَابِعُهُم ... ومنهم من قال بنفي الوصف بالمكان ، وكذلك بالأمكنة كلها إلا على مجاز اللغة بمعنى المحافظ ، والقائم بها ..... قال الشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله : وجملة ذلك أن إضافة كلية الأشياء إليه ، وإضافته عز وجل إليها يخرج مخرج الوصف له بالعلو والرفعة ، ومخرج التعظيم له والجلال الأصل فيه أن الله سبحانه كان ولا مكان، وجائز ارتفاع الأمكنة وبقاؤه على ما كان ، فهو على ما كان ، وكان على ما عليه الآن ، جمل عن التغير والزوال والاستحالة والبطلان ؛ إذ ذلك وأما الأصل عندنا في ذلك أن الله تعالى قال : لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ أمارات الحدث ، فنفى عن نفسه شبه خلقه ، وقد بينا أنه في فعله وصفته متعال عن الأشباه ؛ فيجب القول ' الرحمن على العرش استوى على ما جاء به التنزيل ، وثبت ذلك في العقل ، ثم لا نقطع تأويله على شيء ، لاحتمال غيره مما ذكرنا ونو من وكذلك في كل أمر ثبت التنزيل فيه نحو الرؤية وغير والإيمان بما أراده من غير تحقيق على شيء
Al-Ash'ari took a middle path in the explanation of the Throne (al-‘Arsh) and the Establishment (al-Istiwa). Ibn 'Asakir says: Likewise, al-Najjariyya said that the Creator, glorified is He, is in every place without indwelling (hulul) or direction (jiha). And the Hashwiyya al-Mujassima said that He is indwelling in the Throne, and that the Throne is a place for Him, and He is sitting upon it. So he followed a middle way between them and said: He was without a place, then He created the Throne and the Chair and did not need a place, and He after creating place is as He was before creation. And Maturidi also goes to that effect. We read from Kitab al-Tawhid: Then the people of Islam differed concerning the saying about place. Some of them claimed that He is described as being upon the Throne, and the Throne with them is the couch carried by the encircling angels: 'and those who bear the Throne of your Lord above them on that day, eight' (al-Haqqa 69:17), and His saying: 'And you see the angels encircling around the Throne' (al-Zumar 39:75), and His saying: 'Those who bear the Throne and those around it' (Ghafir 40:7). And they argued for that with His saying: 'The Most Merciful established Himself upon the Throne' (TaHa 20:5), and they say: He came to it after He was not, because of His saying: 'Then He established Himself upon the Throne' (al-A'raf 7:54). And some of them say: He is in every place with His saying: 'There is no secret counsel of three except that He is the fourth of them' (al-Mujadila 58:7). And some of them said by negating the description with place, and likewise with all places except metaphorically in the sense of preservation and overseeing... Abu Mansur (al-Maturidi), may Allah have mercy on him, said: The sum of that is that the attribution of all things to Him, and His attribution to them, takes the form of describing Him with loftiness and highness, and of magnifying Him and majesty. The principle in that is that Allah, glorified is He, was without a place, and it is possible for places to cease while He remains as He was. So He is as He was, and He was as He is now, [far] from change, passing, transformation, and nullification; because that... And the principle with us in that is that Allah, exalted, said: 'There is nothing like Him' (al-Shura 42:11) [as] signs of createdness, and He negated from Himself similarity to His creation. And we have explained that He in His action and attribute is transcendent above likenesses. So it is necessary to say: 'The Most Merciful established Himself upon the Throne' as it came in revelation, and that is established in reason, then we do not cut off its interpretation on any one thing, because of the possibility of other interpretations from what we have mentioned and the like. And likewise in every matter in which revelation is established, such as the vision and other things, we believe in what He intended without determining a specific meaning.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage classifies the differing views on the issue of al-makan (place) and al-istiwa (establishment) and presents the Maturidi-Ash'ari middle path. It begins by quoting Ash'ari's position as reported by Ibn 'Asakir: Ash'ari rejected both the Najjariyya's claim that Allah is in every place without hulul (indwelling) and the Hashwiyya Mujassima's anthropomorphism that He sits on the Throne. Instead, Ash'ari said: 'He was without place, then created the Throne and the Chair and did not need a place, and He after creating place is as He was before creation.' Maturidi also adopts this view. Then Maturidi presents the three Muslim factions: (1) Those who say He is on the Throne as a physical seat, citing verses about angels carrying it and the istiwa verse, and they claim He came to the Throne after not being on it; (2) Those who say He is everywhere, citing the verse about being with the creation in their councils; (3) Those who negate spatial description altogether, except metaphorically as 'preservation.' Then Maturidi gives his own conclusion: The principle is that Allah was without place, and places are contingent; He is not subject to change. The ultimate principle is the Quranic verse 'Laysa kamithlihi shay' (Nothing is like Him), which negates similarity. Therefore, we must affirm the verse 'al-Rahman 'ala al-arsh istawa' as it came in revelation, and it is rationally sound, but we do not settle on a single interpretation because multiple interpretations are possible. This method of tafwid (suspending interpretation) is applied to all ambiguous revealed texts.

Key Terms
عرش
استواء
تفويض
تشبيه
تعيين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Maturidi's tafwid means we do not affirm the meaning of istiwa at all.
Correction: Maturidi affirms that the verse is true and rationally sound; he only suspends a single definitive interpretation, not the reality of the attribute.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why should we not fix a single interpretation of 'al-Rahman 'ala al-arsh istawa'?
A) Because the verse is unclear
B) Because reason cannot accept it
C) Because other interpretations are possible
D) Because we must interpret it metaphorically

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's principle is to affirm the revealed wording of istiwa as true and rationally sound, but to refrain from assigning a single interpretation due to the possibility of other meanings consistent with divine transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'al-Rahman 'ala al-arsh istawa', do you truly submit to the words without demanding to know how? Or does your heart seek a detailed explanation that Allah has not given? Are you willing to remain in that state of trust?
?
Where in your life are you insisting on a 'how' from Allah—about His decree, His wisdom in trials, or His attributes—that He has not revealed? Will you now practice tafwid and say 'I believe in what Allah intended' without needing to grasp every detail?
?
Imagine standing before Allah and He asks you about your belief in His istiwa. Will you be able to say: 'I affirmed what You said and left the interpretation to You'? Or will you have to admit that you went beyond the Book and assigned meanings that were not warranted? Let this question drive you back to the exact words of revelation.

The Principle of Tanzih in Istiwa'
Maturidi explains the meaning of istiwa' and the principle of tanzih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's method for interpreting the verse about Allah's 'istiwa' over the Throne' while preserving divine transcendence.

Core Idea
Maturidi affirms the literal wording but avoids specifying a meaning, because Allah is beyond any spatial attribute.

This lesson introduces Maturidi's approach to one of the most debated verses in Islamic theology: 'The Most Merciful established Himself over the Throne.' Maturidi emphasizes that while we affirm the verse as revealed, we must not assign a specific interpretation that would imply corporeality. His methodology safeguards Allah's transcendence while honoring the revealed text.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic original and its literal translation. Notice how Maturidi frames the discussion with the principle of tanzih.
2
Identify the foundational principle
Find the statement 'كان ولا مكان' (He existed without place). This is key to understanding Maturidi's position on Allah's relationship to space.
3
Examine the verse 'Laysa kamithlihi shay'
Maturidi uses this verse to negate any similarity between Allah and creation. See how he connects this to the method of interpreting ambiguous verses.
4
Understand the ta'wil position
Maturidi says we do not definitively interpret istiwa' as any particular thing. Reflect on why he refrains from specifying an interpretation.
This is a moderate position between tafwid and ta'wil.
5
Apply the method to other texts
Maturidi extends this principle to other matters like ru'ya (seeing Allah). Consider how this consistent methodology preserves transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله : وجملة ذلك أن إضافة كلية الأشياء إليه ، وإضافته عز وجل إليها يخرج مخرج الوصف له بالعلو والرفعة ، ومخرج التعظيم له والجلال الأصل فيه أن الله سبحانه كان ولا مكان، وجائز ارتفاع الأمكنة وبقاؤه على ما كان ، فهو على ما كان ، وكان على ما عليه الآن ، جَلَّ عن التغير والزوال والاستحالة والبطلان ؛ وأما الأصل عندنا في ذلك أن الله تعالى قال : لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ أمارات الحدث ، فنفى عن نفسه شبه خلقه ، وقد بينا أنه في فعله وصفته متعال عن الأشباه ؛ فيجب القول : الرحمن على العرش استوى على ما جاء به التنزيل ، وثبت ذلك في العقل ، ثم لا نقطع تأويله على شيء ، لاحتمال غيره مما ذكرنا ونحو من ذلك ، وكذلك في كل أمر ثبت التنزيل فيه نحو الرؤية وغيرها ، والإيمان بما أراده من غير تحقيق على شيء بما أراد الله به ذلك دون شيء
Shaykh Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The sum of that is that the attribution of all things to Him, and His attribution – exalted and majestic – to them, gives the meaning of describing Him with loftiness and elevation, and gives the meaning of magnifying Him and majesty. The foundation of that is that Allah, glorified be He, existed when there was no place, and it is possible for places to disappear while He remains as He was. So He is as He was, and He was as He is now, exalted above change, perishing, transformation, and annihilation. And the foundation with us in that is that Allah the Exalted said: 'There is nothing like Him' – signs of contingency – so He negated from Himself similarity to His creation. And we have explained that He, in His action and attribute, is exalted above likenesses. So it is necessary to say: 'The Most Merciful established Himself over the Throne' as the revelation came, and that is established in the intellect. Then we do not definitively interpret it as something, because of the possibility of other than it from what we mentioned and the like. And similarly in every matter in which revelation is established, such as seeing [Allah] and others, and belief in what He intended without determining it as something, according to what Allah intended by that, without something.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage defines Maturidi's position on the divine attribute of istiwa' (establishment over the Throne). He begins by stating that attributing all things to Allah and His attributing Himself to things conveys meaning of loftiness and majesty, not physical location. The foundational principle is that Allah existed without place and remains after places vanish, unchanged. He then cites the Quranic verse 'There is nothing like Him' (42:11) as proof that Allah negates similarity to creation. Maturidi insists on affirming the literal wording of 'al-Rahman 'ala al-'Arsh istawa' as revealed and rationally established, but he refrains from assigning a specific interpretation (ta'wil) because other possibilities exist. This same method applies to other ambiguous texts like ru'ya (seeing Allah). The believer affirms what Allah intended without fixing a particular meaning beyond what is revealed.

العرش
التنزيه
التأويل
العلو والرفعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Maturidi either denies the literal meaning of istiwa' or interprets it as 'istila' (conquest).
Correction: Maturidi affirms the literal wording 'al-Rahman 'ala al-'Arsh istawa' as revealed and rationally established, but refrains from assigning a specific interpretation that would imply corporeality.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi in this passage, what is the foundational principle regarding Allah and place?
A) Allah is confined to the Throne.
B) Allah existed when there was no place and remains after places vanish.
C) Allah is everywhere in a literal sense.
D) Allah changes with time.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's method affirms the revealed wording of istiwa' while preserving divine transcendence by refusing to specify a human interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'al-Rahman 'ala al-'Arsh istawa', what image forms in your mind? Are you willing to leave that image undefined, trusting Allah's intent without your own interpretation? What discomfort does that cause you?
?
The passage teaches that Allah was without place and remains beyond change. Does your heart truly accept that Allah is not confined to a direction, or do you secretly imagine Him 'above' in a spatial sense? How does that affect your reverence?
?
If you were to apply Maturidi's method to a current area of confusion in your faith—refusing to assign a meaning beyond what is revealed—what would you gain? What would you lose? Are you willing to embrace the silence?

Ahl al-Sunna's Refutation of Mu'tazila Proofs Against Ru'ya
Ahl al-Sunna refute Mu'tazila interpretation of verses denying ru'ya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ahl al-Sunna reinterpret the key Qur'anic verses used by the Mu'tazila to deny the beatific vision, showing that they actually support its possibility.

Core Idea
The verses the Mu'tazila use to deny ru'ya actually prove it—if you read them correctly.

The Mu'tazila cite three verses to argue that Allah cannot be seen. Ahl al-Sunna respond by showing that each verse, when properly understood, supports the possibility of vision. This lesson walks through their refutations, highlighting the key distinction between idrak (comprehensive perception) and ru'ya (vision), the interpretation of 'lan tarani' as temporary, and the argument from Moses' request and the mountain's stability.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the overall flow of the argument.
2
Identify the three Mu'tazila proofs
The Mu'tazila used verses 6:103, 7:143, and 42:51. Notice that the passage addresses only the first two in detail.
3
Understand the response to 'la tudrikuhu al-absar'
Ahl al-Sunna distinguish idrak (encompassing perception) from ru'ya (vision). The verse negates idrak, not ru'ya. This is the key to their refutation.
4
Understand the response to 'lan tarani'
Ahl al-Sunna interpret 'lan tarani' as a temporary denial in this world, not an absolute impossibility. They argue from Moses' request: if ru'ya were impossible, a prophet would not ask for it, and Allah would have rebuked him. Instead, Allah conditioned vision on the mountain's stability, which is possible.
5
Reflect on the concluding challenge
The passage ends by questioning how the Mu'tazila can claim to know the impossibility of ru'ya while Moses himself was unaware of it. This is a powerful rhetorical conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن الطريف أن يتخذ أهل السنة من الآيات التي احتجت بها المعتزلة نفي الرؤية دليلا على إثبات الرؤية. احتجت المعتزلة على نفي الرؤية بقوله تعالى: لا تُدْرِكْهُ الأَبْصَارُ، وقوله لموسى: لَنْ تَرَانِي، وقوله تعالى: وَمَا كَانَ لِبَشَرٍ أَنْ يُكَلِّمَهُ اللهُ إِلَّا وَحْياً أَوْ مِنْ وَرَاءِ حِجَابٍ. ورأى أهل السنة في قوله تعالى لا تُدْرِكُهُ الأَبْصَارُ دليلاً على إثبات الرؤية، إذ الآية لا تنفي الرؤية وإنما تنفي الإدراك؛ لأن فيه معنى الإحاطة، والله منزه عن الإحاطة والجوانب. أما قوله تعالى لموسى لَنْ تَرَانِي حين سأله رَبِّ أَرِنِي أَنْظُرْ إِلَيْكَ فمعناه أنه لن يراه في الدنيا. ثم لو كان موسى يعلم أن رؤية الله مستحيلة كاستحالة أن يتخذ ولداً أو شريكاً لما سألها؛ إذ كيف يليق بمقام النبوة أن يسأل الله ما لا يليق بجلاله وعظمته، ولكان سؤال موسى جهلاً يبلغ درجة الكفر، ولكان الله نهاه وعاتبه كما نهى نوحاً وعاتب آدم في غير هذا. ولكنه تعالى لم ينهه ولا أيأسه وإنما شرط الرؤية باستقرار الجبل فَإِنِ اسْتَقَرَّ مَكَانَهُ فَسَوْفَ تَرَانِي، واستقرار الجبل أمر ممكن في ذاته، وما شرط بالممكن فهو ممكن. ولقد اندك الجبل فلما تَجَلَّى رَبُّهُ لِلْجَبَلِ جَعَلَهُ دَكّاً وَخَرَّ موسَى صَعِقاً، ليعلم الله أنه لن يراه في الدنيا. ثم كيف يدعي المعتزلة العلم باستحالة الرؤية ويجهلها موسى؟ وهل يليق بمقام النبوة أن يجهل موسى من أمر ربه ما عرفته المعتزلة؟ هذه هي من الحجج البالغة والأدلة الدامغة التي استخلصها أهل السنة من القرآن لإثبات الرؤية.
And it is interesting that Ahl al-Sunna take the verses that the Mu'tazila used to negate vision as evidence for affirming vision. The Mu'tazila argued for the negation of vision by His saying, Exalted is He: 'Vision perceives Him not' (6:103), and His saying to Moses: 'You will not see Me' (7:143), and His saying: 'It is not for any human being that Allah should speak to him except by revelation or from behind a veil' (42:51). And Ahl al-Sunna saw in His saying 'Vision perceives Him not' evidence for affirming vision, because the verse does not negate vision (ru'ya) but rather negates perception (idrāk); because perception implies encompassing, and Allah is transcendent beyond encompassing and directions. As for His saying to Moses 'You will not see Me' when he asked 'My Lord, show me [that I may] look at You,' its meaning is that he will not see Him in this world. Then if Moses knew that vision of Allah is impossible, like the impossibility of Him taking a son or partner, he would not have asked it; for how befits the station of prophethood to ask Allah what is not befitting His majesty and greatness, and Moses' question would have been ignorance reaching the level of disbelief, and Allah would have forbidden him and rebuked him as He forbade Noah and rebuked Adam in other matters. But He, Exalted, did not forbid him nor make him despair, but rather conditioned vision upon the mountain's stability: 'Then if it should remain in place, then you will see Me' (7:143). And the stability of the mountain is a thing possible in itself, and what is conditioned upon the possible is itself possible. And the mountain was crushed: 'And when his Lord manifested Himself to the mountain, He made it level, and Moses fell down struck by thunderbolt' (7:143), so that Allah might know that he will not see Him in this world. Then how can the Mu'tazila claim knowledge of the impossibility of vision while Moses was ignorant of it? And is it befitting for the station of prophethood that Moses be ignorant of his Lord's affair that the Mu'tazila know? These are the conclusive proofs and overwhelming evidences that Ahl al-Sunna extracted from the Noble Qur'an to establish vision.
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage presents the Ahl al-Sunna refutation of the Mu'tazila proofs against ru'ya. It is an objection-and-answer passage structured as a debate. The author begins by noting the irony that Ahl al-Sunna use the very verses cited by the Mu'tazila to deny ru'ya as evidence for it. The Mu'tazila cited three verses: 'لا تُدْرِكْهُ الأَبْصَارُ' (Vision perceives Him not), 'لَنْ تَرَانِي' (You will not see Me), and 'وَمَا كَانَ لِبَشَرٍ أَنْ يُكَلِّمَهُ اللهُ إِلَّا وَحْياً أَوْ مِنْ وَرَاءِ حِجَابٍ' (It is not for any human that Allah speaks to him except by revelation or from behind a veil). The Ahl al-Sunna response: For the first verse, they distinguish between 'idrāk' (comprehensive perception, implying encompassment) and 'ru'ya' (vision). Allah negates idrāk, not ru'ya, because idrāk implies encompassing, which is impossible for Allah. For the second verse (لن تراني), they interpret it as denying vision in this world (al-dunyā), not in the afterlife. They then argue from the fact that Moses asked for vision: if ru'ya were impossible, Moses, a prophet, would not have asked for it. His question would have been ignorance amounting to disbelief, and Allah would have rebuked him. Instead, Allah conditioned vision on the mountain's stability, which is possible, indicating that ru'ya itself is possible. The mountain's destruction upon Allah's manifestation shows that vision is possible but not in this world. The passage concludes by challenging the Mu'tazila claim to knowledge of impossibility, given that Moses was unaware of it. It calls these the conclusive proofs extracted by Ahl al-Sunna from the Quran.

Key Terms
رؤية
إدراك
لا تُدْرِكْهُ الأَبْصَارُ
لن تراني
إحاطة
تجلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the verse 'la tudrikuhu al-absar' negates vision of Allah entirely.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna explain that the verse negates idrak (comprehensive perception/encompassing), not ru'ya. Vision of Allah is possible; it is comprehensive perception that is impossible for Allah.

Checkpoint
How do Ahl al-Sunna interpret the verse 'لا تُدْرِكُهُ الأَبْصَارُ'?
A) It negates vision (ru'ya) of Allah
B) It negates comprehensive perception (idrak) but not vision
C) It applies only to prophets
D) It is abrogated

Key Takeaway
The Qur'anic verses that seem to deny ru'ya actually affirm its possibility when understood correctly.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the phrase 'لا تُدْرِكْهُ الأَبْصَارُ', does your heart immediately assume that seeing Allah is impossible? Or do you pause to consider the precise meaning taught by Ahl al-Sunna? What does your immediate reaction reveal about your reliance on scholars versus your own unchecked understanding? Commit today to always seek the interpretation of the righteous predecessors before drawing conclusions about Allah's attributes.
?
Moses, a prophet, boldly asked to see Allah. Do you have such a burning desire to see your Lord? Or has the world dulled your longing for the vision of Allah in Paradise? Ask yourself: what is one thing you can do today to increase your yearning for ru'ya?
?
The Mu'tazila confidently declared ru'ya impossible, contradicting the very prophet who asked for it. Are you ever quick to assert something about Allah that the prophets themselves did not claim? How can you guard your tongue and heart from overstepping the bounds of Islamic creed? Make a concrete plan to learn the principles of Ahl al-Sunna so that you are not swayed by arguments that contradict revelation.

Divine Transcendence

Rejection of the Term 'Body' for Allah
Prohibits calling Allah 'body' based on tawqif and notes Baqillani's agreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Islamic theology rejects calling Allah a 'body' based on the principle of tawqif (scriptural restriction) and consensus.

Core Idea
Allah's names are revealed, not invented; 'body' is not among them.

This passage from Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid addresses the specific rejection of the term 'body' (جسم) for God. Even if one intends a qualified meaning, the principle of tawqif forbids using names that Allah has not used for Himself. Maturidi states his proof, and later Ash'ari scholar al-Baqillani agrees, citing the consensus of the community.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of tawqif
Recall that in the previous lesson, tawqif means names of Allah are restricted to what is revealed. This passage applies that principle specifically to 'body'.
2
Read Maturidi's argument
Read the Arabic passage and translation to see how Maturidi establishes that 'body' is not among Allah's names and no permission came.
The passage has some OCR issues, but the main argument is clear.
3
Note Baqillani's agreement
Observe that al-Baqillani, from the Ash'ari school, also prohibits 'body' because of consensus.
This shows inter-school agreement on the principle.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why even qualified uses (e.g., 'body unlike bodies') are not allowed.
The principle is strict: we only use what Allah has used.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى ذلك فلا أن نقول بأن الله جسم حتى أردنا به المغايرة أي أن الله جسم لا كا الأجسام أو أردنا لا كالأجسام أو أردنا به الإثبات أو الوجود . يقول الماتريدي : وحقه السمع عن الله ، إن الجسم [ليس] من أسمائه ، ولم يرد أذن لأحد تقليده ، فالقول به لا يسخ ، ولو وسع بالنحت لو هذه ولا عن أحاد ثمن أو سمعي يصح من غير دليل حسبي أو عقلي لوسع القبول بالجسد والشخص ، وكل ذلك مستنكر بالسمع، ويسع القول بكل ما يسمى به الخلق، وذلك فاسد... إذ لا يسمى به الأعراض ويقل : لا أحد يجعل الجسم من أسماء الإثبات والصفات على احد اسم الاثبات، لذلك بطل القول به . وحين جاء الباقلاني، وهو أشعري، ليقول بالتوقيف بعد الماتريدي. لم يقل أكثر مما قاله الماتريدي . منع الباقلاني من إطلاق لفظ الجسم على الله لأن الأمة مجمعة على حظر تسميته مراقبة وفطنا وحافظاً ، وإن كان بمعنى من يستحق هذه التسمية : لأنه لأنه عالم، وليس العقل والحفظ والنطنة والدراية شيئاً أكثر من العلم.
And on that basis, we do not say that Allah is a body, even if we intend by it 'otherness', i.e., Allah is a body unlike bodies, or we intend 'negation of likening', or we intend 'affirmation' or 'existence'. Al-Maturidi says: Its proof is hearing from Allah that 'body' is not among His names, and permission has not come for anyone to imitate [that usage], so saying it is not valid, and if it were allowed by [؟], then this [؟] or heard [؟] would be valid without a sense-based or rational proof, it would allow acceptance of [the term] body and person, and all that is rejected by revelation, and it would allow saying with every [term] used for creation, and that is corrupt... For it is not used for accidents. And he says: No one makes 'body' among the names of affirmation and attributes upon any name of affirmation, so the claim to it is invalid. And when al-Baqillani, who is Ash'ari, came to say [the principle of] tawqif after al-Maturidi, he did not say more than what al-Maturidi said. Al-Baqillani prohibited applying the term 'body' to Allah because the community (umma) is unanimously agreed upon prohibiting naming Him [as] watchful, intelligent, guardian – if it is in the sense of one who deserves these descriptions – because He is all-knowing, and intelligence, memory, perceptiveness, and awareness are nothing more than knowledge.
Source pages p. 579

Commentary
This passage continues the theme of tawqif by specifically rejecting the term 'body' (جسم) for God. It first notes that even if one intends by 'body' something like 'otherness' or 'affirmation', it is not permissible. Maturidi states his proof: it is established by revelation (سمع) that 'body' is not among God's names, and no permission has come to use it; hence saying it is invalid. The passage then notes that al-Baqillani, an Ash'ari scholar, agreed completely, prohibiting 'body' for God because the Muslim community is unanimous in forbidding such names that imply attributes of created beings like being watchful or intelligent in a manner suggesting composition. Baqillani argues that such attributes reduce to knowledge, which is already affirmed of God, so no new meaning is added. Thus, the consensus (ijma') against using 'body' reinforces Maturidi's position.

Key Terms
جسم
توقيف
الإجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'body' could be used by analogy with creatures but with qualification (e.g., 'body unlike bodies').
Correction: The passage clarifies that even qualified use is not permitted because the name is not revealed and there is no permission, and the community has consensus on prohibition.

Checkpoint
Why did Maturidi reject calling Allah 'body'?
A) Because the Quran explicitly declares that Allah is not a body.
B) Because it is not among the names that Allah has named Himself with, and no permission came for it.
C) Because bodies are contingent and cannot exist eternally.
D) Because the Ash'aris prohibit it.

Key Takeaway
Calling Allah a 'body' is impermissible because it is not among His revealed names, and the community has consensus on its prohibition.
